     <p><b>Michigan State University</b> (<b>MSU</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public</a> <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university" class="mw-redirect">research university</a> located in <a href="/wiki/East_Lansing,_Michigan" title="East Lansing, Michigan">East Lansing, Michigan</a>, United States and is the first <a href="/wiki/Land-grant_institution" title="Land-grant institution" class="mw-redirect">land-grant institution</a> that was created to serve as a model for future land-grant colleges in the country under the 1862 <a href="/wiki/Morrill_Land-Grant_Colleges_Act" title="Morrill Land-Grant Colleges Act" class="mw-redirect">Morrill Act</a>.</p> 
     <p>MSU pioneered the studies of <a href="/wiki/Packaging" title="Packaging" class="mw-redirect">packaging</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hospitality_management_studies" title="Hospitality management studies">hospitality business</a>, <a href="/wiki/Supply_chain_management" title="Supply chain management">supply chain management</a>, and telecommunication. Today its <a href="/wiki/Study_abroad" title="Study abroad" class="mw-redirect">study-abroad</a> program is the largest of any single-campus university in the country, offering more than 200 programs in more than 60 countries on all continents including Antarctica.</p> 
     <p>It is considered to be one of America's <a href="/wiki/Public_Ivy" title="Public Ivy">Public Ivy</a> universities, which recognizes top public research universities in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-publicivy_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-publicivy-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> Following the introduction of the <a href="/wiki/Morrill_Act" title="Morrill Act" class="mw-redirect">Morrill Act</a>, the college became <a href="/wiki/Coeducation" title="Coeducation" class="mw-redirect">coeducational</a> and expanded its curriculum beyond agriculture. Today, MSU is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_United_States_university_campuses_by_enrollment" title="List of largest United States university campuses by enrollment" class="mw-redirect">ninth-largest university</a> in the United States, with 47,800 students and 2,954 <a href="/wiki/Faculty_(teaching_staff)" title="Faculty (teaching staff)" class="mw-redirect">faculty</a> members. The school's <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_physics" title="Nuclear physics">nuclear physics</a>, economics, engineering, business, education, <a href="/wiki/Osteopathic_medicine" title="Osteopathic medicine" class="mw-redirect">osteopathic medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Political_science" title="Political science">political science</a>, journalism, <a href="/wiki/Packaging" title="Packaging" class="mw-redirect">packaging</a>, <a href="/wiki/Natural_resource_management" title="Natural resource management">fisheries and wildlife, forestry</a>, and criminal justice programs are among the nation's best.</p> 
     <p>MSU's <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I" title="NCAA Division I" class="mw-redirect">Division I</a> sports teams are called the <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_Spartans" title="Michigan State Spartans">Spartans</a>. They compete in the <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference" title="Big Ten Conference">Big Ten Conference</a> in all sports except ice hockey, in which the team is part of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Collegiate_Hockey_Association" title="Central Collegiate Hockey Association">Central Collegiate Hockey Association</a>. MSU's <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a> <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_Spartans_football" title="Michigan State Spartans football">team</a> won the <a href="/wiki/Rose_Bowl_Game" title="Rose Bowl Game">Rose Bowl</a> in 1954, 1956 and 1988 and boasts six national championships.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> Its men's basketball team won the <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship">NCAA National Championship</a> in 1979 and 2000 and is currently enjoying a streak of six <a href="/wiki/Final_Four" title="Final Four" class="mw-redirect">Final Four</a> appearances over the last 13 seasons. MSU men's <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> won <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Ice_Hockey_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Ice Hockey Championship">national titles</a> in 1966, 1986 and 2007. Cross country has historically been Michigan State's most successful sport, especially during a four-decade period spanning roughly 1930–1970 during which the Spartans won eight NCAA championships and numerous other conference and national titles.<sup id="cite_ref-Frimodig.2C_L._1971_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frimodig.2C_L._1971-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_Michigan_State_University" title="History of Michigan State University">History of Michigan State University</a>
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture_school">Agriculture school</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Agriculture school">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Land_grant_college_stamp.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Land_grant_college_stamp.jpg/180px-Land_grant_college_stamp.jpg" width="180" height="118" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Land_grant_college_stamp.jpg/270px-Land_grant_college_stamp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b9/Land_grant_college_stamp.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Land_grant_college_stamp.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/United_States_Postal_Service" title="United States Postal Service">USPS</a> commemorative 
        <a href="/wiki/Postage_stamp" title="Postage stamp">stamp</a> showing the first federal land-grant colleges for their states in 1863.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Beaumont_Tower_10_2007_BR.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Beaumont_Tower_10_2007_BR.jpg/170px-Beaumont_Tower_10_2007_BR.jpg" width="170" height="272" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Beaumont_Tower_10_2007_BR.jpg/255px-Beaumont_Tower_10_2007_BR.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Beaumont_Tower_10_2007_BR.jpg/340px-Beaumont_Tower_10_2007_BR.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Beaumont_Tower_10_2007_BR.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Beaumont_Tower" title="Beaumont Tower">Beaumont Tower</a> marks the site of 
        <a href="/wiki/College_Hall_(Michigan_State_University)" title="College Hall (Michigan State University)">College Hall</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Constitution" title="Michigan Constitution" class="mw-redirect">Michigan Constitution</a> of 1850 called for the creation of an &quot;agricultural school&quot;,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> though it was not until February 12, 1855, that Michigan <a href="/wiki/List_of_Governors_of_Michigan" title="List of Governors of Michigan">Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/Kinsley_S._Bingham" title="Kinsley S. Bingham">Kinsley S. Bingham</a> signed a bill establishing the United States' first agriculture college, the Agricultural College of the State of Michigan.<sup id="cite_ref-sesquicentennial_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sesquicentennial-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Classes began on May 13, 1857, with three buildings, five faculty members, and 63 male students. The first president, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_R._Williams" title="Joseph R. Williams">Joseph R. Williams</a>, designed a curriculum that required more scientific study than practically any undergraduate institution of the era. It balanced science, <a href="/wiki/Liberal_arts" title="Liberal arts" class="mw-redirect">liberal arts</a>, and practical training. The curriculum excluded <a href="/wiki/Latin_language" title="Latin language" class="mw-redirect">Latin</a> and Greek studies, since most applicants did not study any classical languages in their rural high schools. However, it did require three hours of daily <a href="/wiki/Manual_labour" title="Manual labour">manual labor</a>, which kept costs down for both the students and the College.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite Williams' innovations and his defense of education for the masses, the State Board of Education saw Williams' curriculum as <a href="/wiki/Elitism" title="Elitism">elitist</a>. They forced him to resign in 1859 and reduced the curriculum to a two-year vocational program.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Land_Grant_pioneer">Land Grant pioneer</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Land Grant pioneer">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In 1860, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_R._Williams" title="Joseph R. Williams">Joseph R. Williams</a> became acting <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_governor" title="Lieutenant governor">lieutenant governor</a><sup id="cite_ref-josephrwilliams_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-josephrwilliams-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> and helped pass the Reorganization Act of 1861. This gave the College a four-year curriculum and the power to grant master's degrees. Under the act, a newly created body, known as the State Board of Agriculture, took over from the State Board of Education in running the institution.<sup id="cite_ref-sesquicentennial_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sesquicentennial-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> The College changed its name to State Agricultural College, and its first class graduated in the same year. As the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">Civil War</a> had just begun, there was no time for an elaborate graduation ceremony. The first alumni enlisted to the <a href="/wiki/Union_Army" title="Union Army">Union Army</a>. Williams died, and the following year, <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Abraham Lincoln</a> signed the First <a href="/wiki/Morrill_Act" title="Morrill Act" class="mw-redirect">Morrill Act</a> of 1862 to support similar colleges, making the Michigan school a national model.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oakland_University">Oakland University</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Oakland University">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In 1957, the donation of 1,500 acres (6.1&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>) in Pontiac Township, Michigan prompted creation of Michigan State University – Oakland. This donation was indicative of the University's benefactor community that continues today. That campus became officially independent in 1970 as <a href="/wiki/Oakland_University" title="Oakland University">Oakland University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Oakland_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oakland-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Co-ed_college">Co-ed college</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Co-ed college">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Cowles_House_10_2007_BR.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f0/Cowles_House_10_2007_BR.jpg/220px-Cowles_House_10_2007_BR.jpg" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f0/Cowles_House_10_2007_BR.jpg/330px-Cowles_House_10_2007_BR.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f0/Cowles_House_10_2007_BR.jpg/440px-Cowles_House_10_2007_BR.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Cowles_House_10_2007_BR.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Alice B Cowles House is the official home of the university president and is the oldest existing building on campus.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The college first admitted women in 1870, although at that time there were no female residence halls. The few women who enrolled either boarded with faculty families or made the arduous <a href="/wiki/Stagecoach" title="Stagecoach">stagecoach</a> trek from Lansing. From the early days, female students took the same rigorous scientific agriculture courses as male students. In 1896, the faculty created a &quot;Women Course&quot; that melded a <a href="/wiki/Family_and_consumer_science" title="Family and consumer science">home economics</a> curriculum with <a href="/wiki/Liberal_arts" title="Liberal arts" class="mw-redirect">liberal arts</a> and sciences. That same year, the College turned the old Abbot Hall male dorm into a women's dormitory. It was not until 1899 that the State Agricultural College admitted its first African American student, William O. Thompson. After graduation, he taught at what is now <a href="/wiki/Tuskegee_University" title="Tuskegee University">Tuskegee University</a>. President <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_L._Snyder" title="Jonathan L. Snyder">Jonathan L. Snyder</a> invited its president <a href="/wiki/Booker_T._Washington" title="Booker T. Washington">Booker T. Washington</a> to be the Class of 1900 commencement speaker. A few years later, Myrtle Craig became the first woman African-American student to enroll at the College. Along with the Class of 1907, she received her degree from U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">Theodore Roosevelt</a>, commencement speaker for the Semi-Centennial celebration. The City of East Lansing was incorporated in that same year,<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> and two years later the college officially changed its name to Michigan Agricultural College (M.A.C.).</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Big_Ten_university">Big Ten university</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Big Ten university">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>During the early 20th century, M.A.C. expanded its curriculum well beyond agriculture. By 1925 it had expanded enough that it changed its name to Michigan State College of Agriculture and Applied Science (M.S.C.). In 1941 the Secretary of the State Board of Agriculture, <a href="/wiki/John_A._Hannah" title="John A. Hannah">John A. Hannah</a>, became president of the College. He began the largest expansion in the institution's history, with the help of the 1945 <a href="/wiki/G._I._Bill_of_Rights" title="G. I. Bill of Rights" class="mw-redirect">G.I. Bill</a>, which helped World War II veterans to receive an education. One of Hannah's strategies was to build a new dormitory building, enroll enough students to fill it, and use the income to start construction on a new dormitory. Under his plan, enrollment increased from 15,000 in 1950 to 38,000 in 1965.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1957 Hannah continued MSU's expansion by co-founding Michigan State University–Oakland, now <a href="/wiki/Oakland_University" title="Oakland University">Oakland University</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Matilda_Dodge_Wilson" title="Matilda Dodge Wilson">Matilda Dodge Wilson</a>. Hannah also got the chance to improve the athletic reputation of M.S.C. when the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago" title="University of Chicago">University of Chicago</a> resigned from the <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference" title="Big Ten Conference">Big Ten Conference</a> in 1946. Hannah lobbied hard to take its place, gaining admission in 1949.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> Six years later, in its Centennial year of 1955, the State of Michigan renamed the College as Michigan State University of Agriculture and Applied Science.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> Nine years after that, the University governing body changed its name from the State Board of Agriculture to the MSU Board of Trustees. The State of Michigan<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> allowed the University to drop the words &quot;Agriculture and Applied Science&quot; from its name. Since 1964 the institution has gone by the name of Michigan State University.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_leader_by_2012">Global leader by 2012</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Global leader by 2012">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Cyclotron.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/MSU_Cyclotron.jpg/220px-MSU_Cyclotron.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/MSU_Cyclotron.jpg/330px-MSU_Cyclotron.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/MSU_Cyclotron.jpg/440px-MSU_Cyclotron.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Cyclotron.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/National_Superconducting_Cyclotron_Laboratory" title="National Superconducting Cyclotron Laboratory">National Superconducting Cyclotron Laboratory</a> features one of the most powerful instruments of its type in the world.
        <sup id="cite_ref-Bruns_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bruns-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Since the end of the Hannah era, Michigan State has shifted its focus from increasing the size of its student body to advancing its national and global reputation. In September 2005, current president <a href="/wiki/Lou_Anna_Simon" title="Lou Anna Simon">Lou Anna Simon</a> called for MSU, one of the <a href="/wiki/Public_Ivy" title="Public Ivy">public ivy institutions</a>, to become the global model leader for Land Grant institutions by the year 2012. Her plans include creating a new <a href="/wiki/Residential_college" title="Residential college">residential college</a> and increasing grants awarded from the <a href="/wiki/National_Institutes_of_Health" title="National Institutes of Health">National Institutes of Health</a> past the US$100 million mark. While there are over 100 <a href="/wiki/Land-grant_universities" title="Land-grant universities" class="mw-redirect">Land-grant universities</a> in the United States, she has stated that she would like Michigan State University to be the leader.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Michigan State, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Michigan" title="University of Michigan">University of Michigan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wayne_State_University" title="Wayne State University">Wayne State University</a> created the <a href="/wiki/University_Research_Corridor" title="University Research Corridor">University Research Corridor</a> in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-MSU-university-research-corridor_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSU-university-research-corridor-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> This alliance was formed to transform and strengthen Michigan's economy by reaching out to businesses, policymakers, innovators, investors and the public to speed up technology transfer, make resources more accessible and help attract new jobs to the state.<sup id="cite_ref-MSU-university-research-corridor_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSU-university-research-corridor-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Campus_of_Michigan_State_University" title="Campus of Michigan State University">Campus of Michigan State University</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Campus_Map_small_rev3.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/MSU_Campus_Map_small_rev3.png/220px-MSU_Campus_Map_small_rev3.png" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/MSU_Campus_Map_small_rev3.png/330px-MSU_Campus_Map_small_rev3.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/MSU_Campus_Map_small_rev3.png/440px-MSU_Campus_Map_small_rev3.png 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Campus_Map_small_rev3.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> MSU's main campus lies north of the CN Railway and south of Michigan and Grand River Avenues.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>MSU's sprawling campus is located in <a href="/wiki/East_Lansing,_Michigan" title="East Lansing, Michigan">East Lansing</a>, Michigan. The campus is perched on the banks of the <a href="/wiki/Red_Cedar_River_(Michigan)" title="Red Cedar River (Michigan)">Red Cedar River</a>. Development of the campus started in 1856 with three buildings: a multipurpose building called <a href="/wiki/College_Hall_(Michigan_State_University)" title="College Hall (Michigan State University)">College Hall</a>, a dormitory later called &quot;<a href="/wiki/Saints%27_Rest" title="Saints' Rest">Saints' Rest</a>&quot;,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> and a barn. Today, MSU's contiguous campus consists of 5,200 acres (21&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>), 2,000 acres (8.1&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>) of which are developed. There are 556 buildings: 100 for academics, 131 for agriculture, 166 for housing and <a href="/wiki/Food_service" title="Food service" class="mw-redirect">food service</a>, and 42 for athletics. Overall, the university has 22,763,025 square feet (2,114,754.2&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>) of total indoor space.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> Connecting it all is 26 miles (42&nbsp;km) of roads and 100 miles (160&nbsp;km) of sidewalks.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> MSU also owns 44 non-campus properties, totaling 22,000 acres (89&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>) in 28 different counties.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Beaumont_Tower_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a2/MSU_Beaumont_Tower_1.jpg/220px-MSU_Beaumont_Tower_1.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a2/MSU_Beaumont_Tower_1.jpg/330px-MSU_Beaumont_Tower_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a2/MSU_Beaumont_Tower_1.jpg/440px-MSU_Beaumont_Tower_1.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Beaumont_Tower_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> View of Beaumont Tower from the north.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_campus">North campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: North campus">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The oldest part of campus lies on the north bank of the Red Cedar.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>It includes <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_Gothic" title="Collegiate Gothic" class="mw-redirect">Collegiate Gothic</a> architecture, plentiful trees, and curving roads with few straight lines. It was in this area that the College built its first three buildings, of which none survive. Other historic buildings north of the river include <a href="/wiki/Cowles_House_(East_Lansing,_Michigan)" title="Cowles House (East Lansing, Michigan)">Cowles House</a>, the president's official residence, and <a href="/wiki/Beaumont_Tower" title="Beaumont Tower">Beaumont Tower</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Carillon" title="Carillon">carillon</a> clock tower marking the site of <a href="/wiki/College_Hall_(Michigan_State_University)" title="College Hall (Michigan State University)">College Hall</a>, the original classroom building. To the east lies <a href="/wiki/Eustace_Hall" title="Eustace Hall">Eustace–Cole Hall</a>, America's first freestanding laboratory for horticulture.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> Other landmarks include the bronze statue of former president <a href="/wiki/John_A._Hannah" title="John A. Hannah">John A. Hannah</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/W._J._Beal_Botanical_Garden" title="W. J. Beal Botanical Garden">W. J. Beal Botanical Garden</a>, and the painted boulder known as &quot;<a href="/wiki/The_Rock_(Michigan_State_University)" title="The Rock (Michigan State University)">The Rock</a>&quot;, which is a popular spot for theatre, <a href="/wiki/Tailgate_party" title="Tailgate party">tailgating</a>, and candlelight vigils. On the northwest corner of campus lies the University's hotel, the Kellogg Hotel and Conference Center. The university also has a museum, initiated in 1857. MSU Museum is one of the oldest museums in the Midwest and is accredited by the American Alliance of Museums.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_campus">South campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: South campus">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Wharton_Center.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/MSU_Wharton_Center.jpg/220px-MSU_Wharton_Center.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/MSU_Wharton_Center.jpg/330px-MSU_Wharton_Center.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/MSU_Wharton_Center.jpg/440px-MSU_Wharton_Center.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Wharton_Center.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Wharton_Center_for_Performing_Arts" title="Wharton Center for Performing Arts">Wharton Center for Performing Arts</a> hosts many productions throughout the year and was host to the final US Presidential Debate before the 1992 election.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><br /></p> 
     <p>The campus south of the river consists mostly of post-World War II <a href="/wiki/International_Style_(architecture)" title="International Style (architecture)">International Style</a> buildings with sparse foliage, relatively straight roadways, and numerous parking lots. The &quot;2020 Vision&quot; Master Plan proposes replacing these parking lots with <a href="/wiki/Multi-storey_car_park" title="Multi-storey car park">parking ramps</a> and green space,<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> but these plans will take many years to reach fruition. As part of the master plan, the University erected a new bronze statue of <i><a href="/wiki/Sparty" title="Sparty">The Spartan</a></i> in 2005 to be placed at the intersection of Chestnut and Kalamazoo, just south of the Red Cedar River. This replica replaced the original <a href="/wiki/Modernist" title="Modernist" class="mw-redirect">modernist</a> <a href="/wiki/Terra_cotta" title="Terra cotta" class="mw-redirect">terra cotta</a> statue,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> which can still be seen inside <a href="/wiki/Spartan_Stadium,_East_Lansing" title="Spartan Stadium, East Lansing" class="mw-redirect">Spartan Stadium</a>. Notable academic and research buildings on the South Campus include the <a href="/wiki/National_Superconducting_Cyclotron_Laboratory" title="National Superconducting Cyclotron Laboratory">Cyclotron</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_University_College_of_Law" title="Michigan State University College of Law">College of Law</a>.</p> 
     <p>This part of campus is home to the <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_University_Horticulture_Gardens" title="Michigan State University Horticulture Gardens">MSU Horticulture Gardens</a> and the adjoining <a href="/wiki/4-H" title="4-H">4-H</a> Children's Garden. South of the gardens lie the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_National" title="Canadian National" class="mw-redirect">Canadian National</a> and <a href="/wiki/CSX_Transportation" title="CSX Transportation">CSX</a> railroads, which divide the main campus from thousands of acres of university-owned farmland. The university's agricultural facilities include the Horse, Dairy Cattle, Beef Cattle, Sheep, and Poultry Teaching and Research Farms, as well as the Air Quality Control Lab and the Diagnostics Center for Population and Animal Health.<br style="clear:both;" /></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dubai_Campus">Dubai Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Dubai Campus">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In 2007, Michigan State University established an education center in <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a>, United Arab Emirates. The chief officer of the campus was <a href="/wiki/Brendan_Mullen_(politician)" title="Brendan Mullen (politician)" class="mw-redirect">Brendan Mullen,</a> Dean, Michigan State University Dubai. MSU Dubai was the first American university with a presence in <a href="/wiki/Dubai_International_Academic_City" title="Dubai International Academic City">Dubai International Academic City</a>, with classes beginning in August 2008. The University offered six undergraduate programs: Business Administration; Child and Youth Development; Construction Project Management; Early Childhood Education; Media Management and Research; Computer Engineering, which later was changed to Electrical and Computer Engineering; and a Master's Degree in Human Resources &amp; Labor Relations. The University attracted 100 students from all over the Middle East and beyond.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> However, in 2010 MSU closed the program and the campus because of low enrollment, before any students had graduated. MSU made plans for the existing students to transfer either to the main campus in East Lansing or to other universities in the UAE.<sup id="cite_ref-CHE2010_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CHE2010-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> MSU said the program would have needed 100–150 new students admitted each year to be viable, but was able to recruit only one-third of that number.<sup id="cite_ref-npr_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-npr-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CHE2012_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CHE2012-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>MSU Dubai currently runs a small campus at <a href="/wiki/Dubai_Knowledge_Village" title="Dubai Knowledge Village">Dubai Knowledge Village</a>. It offered at first only one program, a master's program in human resources and labor relation. In 2011 in added a master's programs in Public Health. In April 2012, MSU Dubai announced that it hopes to begin in 2013 two program in law: a LL.M program as well as a Master of Jurisprudence program.<sup id="cite_ref-CHE2012_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CHE2012-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kellogg_Hotel_and_Conference_Center">Kellogg Hotel and Conference Center</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Kellogg Hotel and Conference Center">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The Kellogg Hotel and Conference Center doubles as a 4-star hotel and a business friendly conference center. It is located on the northwest corner of Michigan State University's campus, across from the <a href="/wiki/Brody_Complex" title="Brody Complex" class="mw-redirect">Brody Complex</a>, on Harrison Road just south of Michigan Avenue. The hotel has 160 rooms and suites which can accommodate anyone staying in East Lansing for a business conference, sporting event or an on-campus visit, but it originally served as a dormitory for MSU students. Besides a lodging facility, the Kellogg Hotel and Conference Center serves as a &quot;learning laboratory for the 300–400 students each year that are enrolled in The School of Hospitality Business and other majors.&quot; The Kellogg Hotel and Conference Center strives to facilitate education by hosting conferences and seminars.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_University_academics" title="Michigan State University academics">Michigan State University academics</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_University_Libraries" title="Michigan State University Libraries">Michigan State University Libraries</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Library_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/MSU_Library_1.jpg/220px-MSU_Library_1.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/MSU_Library_1.jpg/330px-MSU_Library_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/MSU_Library_1.jpg/440px-MSU_Library_1.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Library_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_University_Libraries" title="Michigan State University Libraries">The MSU Library</a> is located on the oldest part of campus between 
        <a href="/wiki/Beaumont_Tower" title="Beaumont Tower">Beaumont Tower</a> and the river.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>MSU has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_US_universities_by_enrollment" title="List of largest US universities by enrollment" class="mw-redirect">ninth largest</a> student body in the U.S. For the fiscal year of 2009–10, the Office of the Registrar conferred 11,140 degrees.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> The student body is 55% female and 45% male. While 89% of students come from all 83 counties in the State of Michigan,<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> also represented are all 50 states in the U.S. and about 130 other countries.<sup id="cite_ref-msufacts_3-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-msufacts-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011–2012 5,898 international students enrolled at MSU. The top five countries represented: <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Korea" title="Korea">Korea</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>. <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://oiss.isp.msu.edu/about_stats.php">[11]</a> MSU has about 4,500 faculty and 6,000 staff members, and a student/faculty ratio of 19:1.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> Listed as a <a href="/wiki/Public_Ivy" title="Public Ivy">Public Ivy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> Michigan State is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a>. Michigan State University <a href="/wiki/Ombudsman" title="Ombudsman">Ombudsman</a> is the longest continually operating ombudsman office at a college or university in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Albert_Fert" title="Albert Fert">Albert Fert</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Adjunct_professor" title="Adjunct professor" class="mw-redirect">Adjunct professor</a> at MSU, was awarded the 2007 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics" title="Nobel Prize in Physics">Nobel Prize in Physics</a> together with <a href="/wiki/Peter_Gr%C3%BCnberg" title="Peter Gr&uuml;nberg">Peter Gr&uuml;nberg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> MSU's <a href="/wiki/Study_abroad" title="Study abroad" class="mw-redirect">study abroad</a> program is the largest of any single-campus university in the United States with 2,461 students studying abroad in 2004–2005 in over 60 countries on all continents, including Antarctica.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> MSU has six faculty members elected to the National Academy of Sciences (NAS); Martin Bukovac (1983), James Dye (1989), Pamela Fraker (2007), Richard Lenski (2006), Michael Thomashow (2003), and James Tiedje (2003).<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Its admissions are difficult; for 2009's entering class, the 25th/75th percentiles for the SAT were 1030 and 1240/1600, and its 25th/75th percentiles on the ACT were 23 and 27/36.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rankings">Rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Rankings">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <table class="infobox vcard" style="width: 22em">

       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <th><i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Rankings_THES_W_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rankings_THES_W-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></th>

       </tr> 
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <p>Michigan State ranks 96th in the world, according to the <a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a>, which measures scientific research.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i> ranks MSU 72nd in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> The 2011 <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a> placed Michigan State University at 164th internationally.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university has over 200 academic programs. <i>U.S. News</i> has ranked MSU's graduate-level elementary education&quot;,<sup id="cite_ref-elementaryed_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elementaryed-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> secondary education,<sup id="cite_ref-secondaryed_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-secondaryed-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Industrial_and_Organizational_Psychology" title="Industrial and Organizational Psychology" class="mw-redirect">Industrial and Organizational Psychology</a><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> programs No.1 for the last 14 years. The National Communication Association (NCA) ranks MSU's PhD programs as No. 1 in educating researchers in the rapidly growing fields of health communication and communication technology.</p> 
     <p>MSU is also ranked number four in several other fields, including international/intercultural communication, mass communication, and interpersonal communication based on the November 2004 NCA report.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Eli Broad College of Business was ranked No. 9 among public institutions and No. 20 nationally in 2010 by <i>Business Week</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> The 2008 <i>U.S. News</i> ranked Michigan State's <a href="/wiki/Supply_Chain_Management" title="Supply Chain Management" class="mw-redirect">Supply Chain Management</a> program in the Eli Broad College of Business No.1 in the nation for the second year in a row.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, the Eli Broad College of Business undergraduate accounting program is ranked 11th overall and 9th among public schools, the graduate accounting program is ranked 8th overall and 6th among public schools, and the doctoral program is ranked 8th overall and 5th among public schools according to the 2010 <i><a href="/wiki/Public_Accounting_Report" title="Public Accounting Report">Public Accounting Report</a>'</i>s Annual Survey of Accounting Professors.<sup id="cite_ref-MSU-rankings-broad-accounting_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSU-rankings-broad-accounting-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The College of Communication Arts and Sciences was established in 1955 and was the first of its kind in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-MSU-rankings-comarts_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSU-rankings-comarts-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> The college's Media and Information Studies doctoral program was ranked No. 2 in 2007 by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Chronicle_of_Higher_Education" title="The Chronicle of Higher Education">The Chronicle of Higher Education</a></i> in the category of mass communication.<sup id="cite_ref-MSU-rankings-comarts_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSU-rankings-comarts-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> The communication doctoral program was ranked No. 4 in a separate category of communication in <i>The Chronicle of Higher Education'</i>s 2005 Faculty Scholarly Productivity Index, published in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-MSU-rankings-comarts_62-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSU-rankings-comarts-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> The college's faculty and alumni include eight <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> winners and a two-time <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Award" title="Emmy Award">Emmy Award</a> winning recording mixer.<sup id="cite_ref-MSU-rankings-comarts_62-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSU-rankings-comarts-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>MSU's graduate program in <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_physics" title="Nuclear physics">nuclear physics</a> is ranked No. 1 in the nation by U.S. News. In <a href="/wiki/Primary_care" title="Primary care">primary medical care</a>, <i>U.S. News</i> ranks MSU's College of Osteopathic Medicine at No.5, College of <a href="/wiki/Veterinary_Medicine" title="Veterinary Medicine" class="mw-redirect">Veterinary Medicine</a> at No.9, and the College of Human Medicine at No.18.<sup id="cite_ref-gradrankings_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gradrankings-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> MSU's graduate program in Mathematics has been ranked 23rd in the US according to the latest National Research Council ranking.</p> 
     <p>Other programs of note include <a href="/wiki/Criminal_justice" title="Criminal justice">criminal justice</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hospitality_management_studies" title="Hospitality management studies">hospitality business</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Packaging" title="Packaging" class="mw-redirect">packaging</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Political_science" title="Political science">political science</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dietetics" title="Dietetics" class="mw-redirect">dietetics</a><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> and communications.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> The Sustainable Endowments Institute awarded Michigan State with an overall grade of &quot;B&quot; on the 2009 Campus Sustainability Survey, including &quot;A&quot;s in the categories of Administration, Transportation, Endowment Transparency, and Investment Policies.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Computer_Center.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/MSU_Computer_Center.jpg/220px-MSU_Computer_Center.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/MSU_Computer_Center.jpg/330px-MSU_Computer_Center.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/MSU_Computer_Center.jpg/440px-MSU_Computer_Center.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Computer_Center.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Computer Center once housed the early research computer 
        <a href="/wiki/MISTIC" title="MISTIC">MISTIC</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The university spent nearly US$405 million in 2008–09 on research,<sup id="cite_ref-msufacts_3-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-msufacts-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> capping a long history of academic research. In 1877, botany professor <a href="/wiki/William_J._Beal" title="William J. Beal" class="mw-redirect">William J. Beal</a> performed the first documented genetic crosses to produce hybrid <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">corn</a>, which led to increased yields. MSU dairy professor <a href="/wiki/G._Malcolm_Trout" title="G. Malcolm Trout">G. Malcolm Trout</a> invented the process for the <a href="/wiki/Homogenization_(chemistry)" title="Homogenization (chemistry)">homogenization</a> of milk in the 1930s. In the 1960s, MSU scientists developed <a href="/wiki/Cisplatin" title="Cisplatin">cisplatin</a>, a leading cancer fighting drug.<br /> Today Michigan State continues its research with facilities such as the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Energy" title="United States Department of Energy">U.S. Department of Energy</a>-sponsored MSU-DOE Plant Research Laboratory<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> and a <a href="/wiki/Particle_accelerator" title="Particle accelerator">particle accelerator</a> called the <a href="/wiki/National_Superconducting_Cyclotron_Laboratory" title="National Superconducting Cyclotron Laboratory">National Superconducting Cyclotron Laboratory</a>. The U.S. Department of Energy Office of Science named Michigan State University as the site for the <a href="/wiki/Facility_for_Rare_Isotope_Beams" title="Facility for Rare Isotope Beams">Facility for Rare Isotope Beams</a> (FRIB). The $550 million facility will attract top researchers from around the world to conduct experiments in basic nuclear science, astrophysics, and applications of isotopes to other fields.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Vet_Research_Farm.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/7e/MSU_Vet_Research_Farm.jpg/220px-MSU_Vet_Research_Farm.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/7e/MSU_Vet_Research_Farm.jpg/330px-MSU_Vet_Research_Farm.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/7e/MSU_Vet_Research_Farm.jpg/440px-MSU_Vet_Research_Farm.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Vet_Research_Farm.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Veterinary Research Farm.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 2004, scientists at the Cyclotron produced and observed a new isotope of the element <a href="/wiki/Germanium" title="Germanium">germanium</a>, called Ge-60<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> In that same year, Michigan State, in consortium with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Carolina_at_Chapel_Hill" title="University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill">University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill</a> and the government of <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, broke ground on the 4.1-meter <a href="/wiki/SOAR_Telescope" title="SOAR Telescope" class="mw-redirect">Southern Astrophysical Research Telescope</a> (SOAR) in the <a href="/wiki/Andes_Mountains" title="Andes Mountains" class="mw-redirect">Andes Mountains</a> of <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>. The consortium telescope will allow the Physics &amp; Astronomy department to study galaxy formation and origins.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> Since 1999, MSU has been part of another consortium called the <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Life_Sciences_Corridor" title="Michigan Life Sciences Corridor">Michigan Life Sciences Corridor</a>, which aims to develop <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">biotechnology</a> research in the State of Michigan.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> Finally, the College of Communication Arts and Sciences' <a href="/wiki/Quello_Center_for_Telecommunication_Management_and_Law" title="Quello Center for Telecommunication Management and Law">Quello Center</a> researches current issues of information and communication management.</p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Big_Ten_Committee_on_Institutional_Cooperation">Big Ten Committee on Institutional Cooperation</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Big Ten Committee on Institutional Cooperation">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>Michigan State University is a participant in the <a href="/wiki/Committee_on_Institutional_Cooperation" title="Committee on Institutional Cooperation">Committee on Institutional Cooperation</a>. The Committee on Institutional Cooperation (CIC) is the academic consortium of the universities in the <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference" title="Big Ten Conference">Big Ten Conference</a> plus former conference member, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago" title="University of Chicago">University of Chicago</a>. The initiative also allows students at participating institutions to take distance courses at other participating institutions. The initiative also forms a partnership of research. Engaging in $8 billion in research in 2010, CIC universities are providing powerful insight into important issues in medicine, technology, agriculture, and communities.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> Students at participating schools are also allowed &quot;in-house&quot; viewing privileges at other participating schools' libraries.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> They also employ collective purchasing, which has saved member institutions $19 million to date.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Endowment">Endowment</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Endowment">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>MSU's (private, non-Morrill Act) <a href="/wiki/Financial_endowment" title="Financial endowment">endowment</a> started in 1916 when the Engineering Building burned down. Automobile magnate <a href="/wiki/R.E._Olds" title="R.E. Olds" class="mw-redirect">R.E. Olds</a> helped the program stay afloat with a gift of $100,000.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> There was a time when MSU lagged behind peer institutions in terms of endowments. As recently as the early 1990s, MSU was last among the eleven Big Ten schools, with barely over $100 million in endowment funds. This changed dramatically in the 2000s (decade), when the University started a campaign to increase the size of the endowment. At the close of <a href="/wiki/Fiscal_year" title="Fiscal year">fiscal year</a> 2004–2005, the endowment had risen to $1.325 billion, raising the University to sixth of the 11 Big Ten schools in terms of endowment; within $2 million of the fifth-rated school.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> The rapid increase in the size of the endowment will help to improve outdated facilities, such as the Music Building, which the College of Music hopes to soon replace with money from its alumni fundraising program.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges">Colleges</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Colleges">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_South_Campus_skyline.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/MSU_South_Campus_skyline.jpg/220px-MSU_South_Campus_skyline.jpg" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/MSU_South_Campus_skyline.jpg/330px-MSU_South_Campus_skyline.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/MSU_South_Campus_skyline.jpg/440px-MSU_South_Campus_skyline.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_South_Campus_skyline.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The South Campus skyline
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>MSU has over 200 academic programs offered by 17-degree granting colleges.<sup id="cite_ref-msufacts_3-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-msufacts-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Residential_colleges">Residential colleges</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Residential colleges">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>MSU has several <a href="/wiki/Residential_colleges" title="Residential colleges" class="mw-redirect">residential colleges</a>, based on the <a href="/wiki/Oxbridge" title="Oxbridge">Oxbridge</a> &quot;living-learning&quot; model. By putting classes in student dormitories, these colleges improve student access to faculty and facilities. MSU's first residential college, <a href="/wiki/Justin_Morrill" title="Justin Morrill" class="mw-redirect">Justin Morrill</a> College started in 1965 with an interdisciplinary curriculum.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> MSU closed Morrill College in 1979, but today the university has three residential colleges, including the recent opening of the <a href="/wiki/Residential_College_in_Arts_%26_Humanities" title="Residential College in Arts &amp; Humanities">Residential College in Arts &amp; Humanities</a> (RCAH) located in Snyder and Phillips halls.</p> 
     <p>Established in 1967, <a href="/wiki/James_Madison_College" title="James Madison College">James Madison College</a> is a smaller component residential college featuring multidisciplinary programs in the social sciences, founded on a model of liberal education. James Madison College is housed in Case Hall. Classes in the college are small, with an average of 25 students, and most instructors are <a href="/wiki/Tenure" title="Tenure" class="mw-redirect">tenure</a> track faculty. James Madison College has about 1150 students total, with each <a href="/wiki/Freshman" title="Freshman">freshman</a> class containing about 320 students.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> Each of Madison's four <a href="/wiki/Academic_major" title="Academic major">majors</a>—Social Relations and Policy, International Relations, Political Theory and Constitutional Democracy, and Comparative Cultures and Politics<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup>—requires two years of foreign language and one semester of &quot;field experience&quot; in an <a href="/wiki/Intern" title="Intern" class="mw-redirect">internship</a> or study abroad program. Although Madison students make up about 4% of MSU graduates, they represent around 35% of the MSU's <a href="/wiki/Phi_Beta_Kappa_Society" title="Phi Beta Kappa Society">Phi Beta Kappa</a> members.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Phillips_Hall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/MSU_Phillips_Hall.jpg/220px-MSU_Phillips_Hall.jpg" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/MSU_Phillips_Hall.jpg/330px-MSU_Phillips_Hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/MSU_Phillips_Hall.jpg/440px-MSU_Phillips_Hall.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Phillips_Hall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Snyder-Phillips Hall was built in 1947. The building was recently expanded to make room for a new residential college.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Also established in 1967, <a href="/wiki/Lyman_Briggs_College" title="Lyman Briggs College">Lyman Briggs College</a> teaches math and science within social, historical and philosophical contexts.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> Many Lyman Briggs students intend to pursue careers in medicine, but the school supports over 30 coordinate majors, from human biology to computer sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> Lyman Briggs is one of the few colleges that lets undergraduates teach as &quot;Learning Assistants.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>MSU's newest residential college is the <a href="/wiki/Residential_College_in_Arts_%26_Humanities" title="Residential College in Arts &amp; Humanities">Residential College in Arts &amp; Humanities</a>. Founded October 21, 2005,<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> the college provides around 600 <a href="/wiki/Undergraduates" title="Undergraduates" class="mw-redirect">undergraduates</a> with an individualized curriculum in the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_arts" title="Liberal arts" class="mw-redirect">liberal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Visual_arts" title="Visual arts">visual</a> and <a href="/wiki/Performing_arts" title="Performing arts">performing arts</a>. Though all the students will graduate with the same <a href="/wiki/Academic_degree" title="Academic degree">degree</a>, MSU encourages students in the college to get a <a href="/wiki/Double_degree" title="Double degree">second degree</a> or specialization.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> The university houses the new college in a newly renovated Snyder-Phillips Hall, the location of MSU's first residential college, Justin Morrill College.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Law_School_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/MSU_Law_School_1.jpg/220px-MSU_Law_School_1.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/MSU_Law_School_1.jpg/330px-MSU_Law_School_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/MSU_Law_School_1.jpg/440px-MSU_Law_School_1.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Law_School_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The MSU Law School Building
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Professional_schools">Professional schools</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Professional schools">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_University_College_of_Law" title="Michigan State University College of Law">Michigan State University College of Law</a> is an independent, non-profit corporation<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> affiliated<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> with the <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public</a> institution. Founded in Detroit in 1891 as the Detroit College of Law, the law school moved to East Lansing in 1995 becoming an integral part of the university. Students attending MSU College of Law come from 42 states and 13 countries. The law school publishes the Michigan State Law Review,<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> the Michigan State Journal of International Law and the Journal of Medicine and Law. The College of Law is the home of the <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Fieger" title="Geoffrey Fieger">Geoffrey Fieger</a> Trial Practice Institute,<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> the first trial practice institute in the United States. The Intellectual Property and Communications Law program was ranked seventeenth nationally, in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Eli_Broad_College_of_Business" title="Eli Broad College of Business">Eli Broad College of Business</a> has programs in accounting, <a href="/wiki/Information_systems" title="Information systems">information systems</a>, finance, management, marketing and <a href="/wiki/Supply_chain_management" title="Supply chain management">supply chain management</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_School_of_Hospitality_Business" title="The School of Hospitality Business" class="mw-redirect">hospitality business</a>. The school has 4,775 undergraduate students and 776 <a href="/wiki/Graduate_students" title="Graduate students" class="mw-redirect">graduate students</a>. The Eli Broad Graduate School of Management, which <i><a href="/wiki/Business_Week" title="Business Week" class="mw-redirect">Business Week</a></i> magazine ranks 11th among public institutions, offers three <a href="/wiki/MBA" title="MBA" class="mw-redirect">MBA</a> programs, as well as <a href="/wiki/Double_major" title="Double major" class="mw-redirect">joint degrees</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_University_College_of_Law" title="Michigan State University College of Law">College of Law</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> The opening of the <a href="/wiki/Eugene_C._Eppley_Center_for_Graduate_Studies_in_Hotel,_Restaurant_and_Institutional_Management" title="Eugene C. Eppley Center for Graduate Studies in Hotel, Restaurant and Institutional Management" class="mw-redirect">Eugene C. Eppley Center for Graduate Studies in Hotel, Restaurant and Institutional Management</a> brought the first program in the United States to offer a Master of Business Administration degree in Hotel, Restaurant and Institutional Management to MSU.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_University_College_of_Nursing" title="Michigan State University College of Nursing">Michigan State University College of Nursing</a> grants <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Science_in_Nursing" title="Bachelor of Science in Nursing">B.S.N.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Science_in_Nursing" title="Master of Science in Nursing">M.S.N.</a>, and PhD degrees.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medical_schools">Medical schools</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Medical schools">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Msu-chm-secchia-center-evening.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Msu-chm-secchia-center-evening.jpg/220px-Msu-chm-secchia-center-evening.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Msu-chm-secchia-center-evening.jpg/330px-Msu-chm-secchia-center-evening.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Msu-chm-secchia-center-evening.jpg/440px-Msu-chm-secchia-center-evening.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Msu-chm-secchia-center-evening.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> MSU Secchia Center
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_University_College_of_Osteopathic_Medicine" title="Michigan State University College of Osteopathic Medicine">Michigan State University College of Osteopathic Medicine</a> was the world's first publicly funded college of <a href="/wiki/Osteopathic_medicine_in_the_United_States" title="Osteopathic medicine in the United States">osteopathic medicine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> It has a long-standing tradition of retaining its alumni in Michigan to practice – more than two-thirds of the college's graduates remain to practice in Michigan.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> Recently, the Michigan State University Board of Trustees approved a resolution endorsing the expansion of the College of Osteopathic Medicine to two sites in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Michigan" title="Southeast Michigan">southeast Michigan</a>, a move board members and college officials say will not only improve medical education in the state, but also address a projected physician <a href="/wiki/Shortage" title="Shortage" class="mw-redirect">shortage</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup><br /></p> 
     <p>According to U.S. News &amp; World Report, the College of Osteopathic Medicine (<a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Osteopathic_Medicine" title="Doctor of Osteopathic Medicine">D.O. degree</a>) ranked No.17 medical schools in the country for primary care and the College of Human Medicine (MD degree) has regularly ranked among the top forty medical schools in the country for primary care.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_University_College_of_Human_Medicine" title="Michigan State University College of Human Medicine">College of Human Medicine</a> graduates students with Doctor of Medicine <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Medicine" title="Doctor of Medicine">M.D.</a> degrees and is split into seven distinct campuses located in <a href="/wiki/East_Lansing,_Michigan" title="East Lansing, Michigan">East Lansing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kalamazoo,_Michigan" title="Kalamazoo, Michigan">Kalamazoo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flint,_Michigan" title="Flint, Michigan">Flint</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saginaw,_Michigan" title="Saginaw, Michigan">Saginaw</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marquette,_Michigan" title="Marquette, Michigan">Marquette</a>, <a href="/wiki/Traverse_City,_Michigan" title="Traverse City, Michigan">Traverse City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grand_Rapids,_Michigan" title="Grand Rapids, Michigan">Grand Rapids</a>. Each campus is affiliated with local hospitals and other medical facilities professionals in the area.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> For example, the Lansing campus includes <a href="/wiki/Sparrow_Hospital" title="Sparrow Hospital">Sparrow Hospital</a> and <a href="/wiki/McLaren%E2%80%93Greater_Lansing_Hospital" title="McLaren–Greater Lansing Hospital">McLaren–Greater Lansing Hospital</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> The College of Human Medicine has recently gained attention for its expansion into the Grand Rapids area, with the new <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.secchiacenter.com/">Secchia Center</a> completed in the Fall of 2010, that is expected to fuel the growing medical industry in that region.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Though Michigan State has offered courses in veterinary science since its founding, the <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_University_College_of_Veterinary_Medicine" title="Michigan State University College of Veterinary Medicine">College of Veterinary Medicine</a> was not formally established as a four-year, degree-granting program until 1910.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> Ranked ninth in the nation,<sup id="cite_ref-gradrankings_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gradrankings-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> the college has over 170,000 square feet (16,000&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>) of office, teaching, and research space, as well as a veterinary <a href="/wiki/Teaching_hospital" title="Teaching hospital">teaching hospital</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_academic_units">Other academic units</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Other academic units">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In recent years, MSU's music program has grown substantially. Music major enrollment increased more than 97% between 1991 and 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-musicfacts_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-musicfacts-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> In early 2007, this growth led the university board of trustees to spin the music program off into its own college unit: The MSU College of Music.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> The new college faces many new challenges, such as working with limited space<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> and funding.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> Nevertheless, MSU's music college plans on continued success, placing an annual average of 25 graduate students in tenure stream university positions.<sup id="cite_ref-musicfacts_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-musicfacts-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
