     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_University_College_of_Education" title="Michigan State University College of Education">College of Education at Michigan State University</a> offers graduate and undergraduate degrees in several fields, including <a href="/wiki/Counseling" title="Counseling" class="mw-redirect">counseling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Educational_psychology" title="Educational psychology">educational psychology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Special_education" title="Special education">special education</a>, <a href="/wiki/Teacher_education" title="Teacher education">teacher education</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kinesiology" title="Kinesiology">kinesiology</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> The college has had high-ranked programs in elementary,<sup id="cite_ref-elementaryed_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elementaryed-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> educational technology, educational policy, and secondary education.<sup id="cite_ref-secondaryed_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-secondaryed-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, Michigan State ties the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison" title="University of Wisconsin–Madison">University of Wisconsin–Madison</a> for the top spot in <a href="/wiki/Rehabilitation_counseling" title="Rehabilitation counseling">rehabilitation counseling</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> The College of Education is currently housed in Erickson Hall.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Erickson_Hall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Erickson_Hall.jpg/220px-Erickson_Hall.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Erickson_Hall.jpg/330px-Erickson_Hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Erickson_Hall.jpg/440px-Erickson_Hall.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Erickson_Hall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Erickson Hall
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Founded in 1956, the <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_University_Honors_College" title="Michigan State University Honors College">MSU Honors College</a> provides individualized curricula to MSU's top undergraduate students. Though the college has no majors of its own, it has its own <a href="/wiki/Dean_(education)" title="Dean (education)">dean</a> and academic advisers to help Honors students with their educational pursuits. High school students starting at MSU may join the Honors College if they are in the top 5% of their high school graduating class and have either an <a href="/wiki/ACT_(examination)" title="ACT (examination)" class="mw-redirect">ACT</a> score of at least 30 or an <a href="/wiki/SAT" title="SAT">SAT</a> total score of at least 1360.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> Once admitted, students must maintain a 3.20 GPA and complete eight approved honors courses in order to graduate with Honors College designation on their degree.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>After three years of planning, <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_University_College_of_Engineering" title="Michigan State University College of Engineering">The College of Engineering</a> successfully launched the first stages of its Residential Experience for Spartan Engineering, formally known as the Residential Option for Scientists and Engineers (ROSES), the new program is located in Wilson Hall after being housed in Bailey Hall for a number of years. The Residential program essentially combines with a brand new academic component, Cornerstone Engineering, where freshman engineering students not only get an overview of the engineering field(s) but get a hands-on experience along with it.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Global_Engineering_Education" title="Global Engineering Education">Global Engineering</a> is a new subject that is of certain interest for not only the Cornerstone Engineering and Residential Experience programs but for the entire <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_University_College_of_Engineering" title="Michigan State University College of Engineering">College of Engineering</a> at MSU. Engineering in today's society has shown to have a monumental impact on the global economy due to advancements in education, interdependence on economics with infrastructure, computers, transportation, technology and other <a href="/wiki/Manufactured_goods" title="Manufactured goods" class="mw-redirect">manufactured goods</a> as well as Michigan State University's <a href="/wiki/Study_abroad" title="Study abroad" class="mw-redirect">study-abroad</a> program being ranked No. 1 in the nation, allowing for students to experience education and learn cultures in hundreds of countries.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> Also of note is the innovative <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://vipp.isp.msu.edu/">Visiting International Professional Program</a>, which connects professional education to the expertise of Michigan State University, a world leader in global research and leadership training. VIPP creates practical links between the world-class faculty at MSU and global industries, businesses, governments and societies. The newly established Cornerstone Engineering and Residential Experience programs for <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_University_College_of_Engineering" title="Michigan State University College of Engineering">College of Engineering</a> have started programs abroad for more courses in engineering including <a href="/wiki/Study_abroad" title="Study abroad" class="mw-redirect">Study abroad</a> <a href="/wiki/Seminars" title="Seminars" class="mw-redirect">seminars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>MSU currently offers a 30 credit graduate program for Masters in Educational Technology<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> in 3 different formats; completely online,<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> hybrid<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> in East Lansing, Michigan, or overseas. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://edutech.msu.edu/overseas.html">MSU.edu</a> The overseas program is offered at universities around the world. Past locations have included England, France, Switzerland and Thailand. The program lasts one month a summer for three summers, with each summer covering 9 credit hours. One online class is required between the second and third summer. The classes are focused on preparing teachers in integrating technology into their classrooms and helping them understand the affordances and constraints of using different programs. The courses are taught by MSU professors and are open to students around the world.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_Spartans" title="Michigan State Spartans">Michigan State Spartans</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Michigan_State_Spartans_championships" title="List of Michigan State Spartans championships">List of Michigan State Spartans championships</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Michigan State's <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I-A" title="NCAA Division I-A" class="mw-redirect">Division I-A</a> program offers 12 <a href="/wiki/Varsity_team" title="Varsity team">varsity</a> sports for men and 13 for women.<sup id="cite_ref-msufacts_3-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-msufacts-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> Since their teams are called the Spartans, MSU's mascot is a Spartan warrior named <a href="/wiki/Sparty" title="Sparty">Sparty</a>. The university participates in the Big Ten Conference in all varsity sports except ice hockey, which competes in the <a href="/wiki/Central_Collegiate_Hockey_Association" title="Central Collegiate Hockey Association">Central Collegiate Hockey Association</a>. The current athletic director is Mark Hollis, who was promoted to the position on January 1, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> Hollis replaced <a href="/wiki/Ron_Mason" title="Ron Mason">Ron Mason</a>, who served as head hockey coach from 1979 to 2002, retiring with a record total of 924 wins, and a 635–270–69 record at MSU.<sup id="cite_ref-ronmason_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ronmason-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 1888 Michigan State University (then as known as Michigan Agricultural College) along with Olivet, Albion and Hillsdale Colleges was a founding member of the nation's oldest athletic conference, the <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Intercollegiate_Athletic_Association" title="Michigan Intercollegiate Athletic Association">Michigan Intercollegiate Athletic Association</a> (MIAA). MAC left the conference in 1907.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_Spartans_football" title="Michigan State Spartans football">Michigan State Spartans football</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Spartan_Stadium_Facade.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/MSU_Spartan_Stadium_Facade.jpg/220px-MSU_Spartan_Stadium_Facade.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/MSU_Spartan_Stadium_Facade.jpg/330px-MSU_Spartan_Stadium_Facade.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/MSU_Spartan_Stadium_Facade.jpg/440px-MSU_Spartan_Stadium_Facade.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Spartan_Stadium_Facade.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Spartan_Stadium,_East_Lansing" title="Spartan Stadium, East Lansing" class="mw-redirect">Spartan Stadium</a> hosts varsity 
        <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a> games and other events.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">Football</a> has a long tradition at Michigan State. Starting as a club sport in 1884, football gained varsity status in 1896.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> MSU football teams won the <a href="/wiki/Rose_Bowl_Game" title="Rose Bowl Game">Rose Bowl</a> in 1954, 1956 and 1988. The Spartans accounted for four of the top eight selections in the <a href="/wiki/1967_NFL_Draft" title="1967 NFL Draft">1967 NFL Draft</a>, the only time a college football program has accomplished such a feat.</p> 
     <p>Today, the football team competes in <a href="/wiki/Spartan_Stadium,_East_Lansing" title="Spartan Stadium, East Lansing" class="mw-redirect">Spartan Stadium</a>, a renovated 75,005 seat football stadium near the center of campus. The current coach is <a href="/wiki/Mark_Dantonio" title="Mark Dantonio">Mark Dantonio</a>, who was hired on November 27, 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> Dantonio had an 18–17 record in his three-year tenure at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cincinnati" title="University of Cincinnati">University of Cincinnati</a>, including a 1–0 Bowl Game record.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> He led the team in its first season to a 7–6 record. The Spartans played in the Champs Sports Bowl against Boston College on December 28, 2007 and the Capital One Bowl against Georgia on January 1, 2009. MSU's traditional archrival is the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Michigan" title="University of Michigan">University of Michigan</a>, against whom they compete annually for the <a href="/wiki/Paul_Bunyan_Trophy" title="Paul Bunyan Trophy">Paul Bunyan Trophy</a>. Their overall record against the Wolverines currently stands at 32–67–5 and 23–34–2 since 1953 when the Paul Bunyan Trophy was established and MSU joined the Big Ten Conference. Dantonio's Spartans have won 4 of the past 5 contests dating back to 2008. Michigan State is one of three Big Ten teams to have an annual non-conference football game against <a href="/wiki/University_of_Notre_Dame" title="University of Notre Dame">Notre Dame</a>. MSU's record against the Fighting Irish is 25–44–1 but the Spartans have had much success against the Irish recently, becoming the first team ever to win six straight games at Notre Dame Stadium.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2010, the Spartans finished 7–1 (11–2) in conference play were Co-Big Ten Champions along with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Wisconsin" title="University of Wisconsin" class="mw-redirect">University of Wisconsin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_University" title="Ohio State University">Ohio State</a>. In 2011, the Spartans finished 1st in the Legends Division of the Big Ten with a 7–1 (11–3) conference record. While beating Wisconsin (Leaders Division Champions) in regular season play on a last second Hail-Mary pass, they lost in dramatic fashion to the Badgers in the inaugural Big Ten Championship Game played in Indianapolis. Though the Spartans did not win the Big Ten Conference Championship they did gain some revenge by beating the SEC's University of Georgia Bulldogs in the 2012 Outback Bowl. The Spartans outlasted the Bulldogs 33–30 in a triple overtime thriller. Dantonio got his first Bowl victory as the Spartans coach, the team finished the 2011 season with 11 wins. High expectations are growing in East Lansing after back to back 11 win seasons, a first time in Spartan Football history. The Spartan Football final ranking in 2011 was No. 10 USA Today Coaches Poll and No. 11 in the AP.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Breslin_Center.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/MSU_Breslin_Center.jpg/220px-MSU_Breslin_Center.jpg" width="220" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/MSU_Breslin_Center.jpg/330px-MSU_Breslin_Center.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/MSU_Breslin_Center.jpg/440px-MSU_Breslin_Center.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Breslin_Center.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Jack Breslin Student Events Center is home to the men and women's basketball teams.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Men.27s_basketball">Men's basketball</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Men's basketball">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_Spartans_men%27s_basketball" title="Michigan State Spartans men's basketball">Michigan State Spartans men's basketball</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/Category:Michigan_State_Spartans_men%27s_basketball_players" title="Category:Michigan State Spartans men's basketball players">Category:Michigan State Spartans men's basketball players</a>&nbsp;and 
      <a href="/wiki/Category:Michigan_State_Spartans_men%27s_basketball_coaches" title="Category:Michigan State Spartans men's basketball coaches">Category:Michigan State Spartans men's basketball coaches</a>
     </div> 
     <p>MSU's men's basketball team has won the <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship">National Championship</a> twice: in 1979 and again in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1979, <a href="/wiki/Magic_Johnson" title="Magic Johnson">Earvin &quot;Magic&quot; Johnson</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-magicjohnson_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-magicjohnson-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> along with <a href="/wiki/Greg_Kelser" title="Greg Kelser">Greg Kelser</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-gregkelser_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gregkelser-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jay_Vincent" title="Jay Vincent">Jay Vincent</a><sup id="cite_ref-jayvincent_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jayvincent-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> and Mike Brkovich, led the MSU team to a 75–64 win against the <a href="/wiki/Larry_Bird" title="Larry Bird">Larry Bird</a>-led <a href="/wiki/Indiana_State_University" title="Indiana State University">Indiana State</a> Sycamores. In 2000, three players from <a href="/wiki/Flint,_Michigan" title="Flint, Michigan">Flint</a>, <a href="/wiki/Morris_Peterson" title="Morris Peterson">Morris Peterson</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-morrispeterson_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-morrispeterson-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Bell_(basketball)" title="Charlie Bell (basketball)">Charlie Bell</a><sup id="cite_ref-charliebell_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charliebell-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Mateen_Cleaves" title="Mateen Cleaves">Mateen Cleaves</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-mateencleaves_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mateencleaves-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> led the team to its second national title. Dubbed the &quot;Flintstones&quot;, they were the key to the Spartans' win against the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida" title="University of Florida">University of Florida</a>. On December 13, 2003, Michigan State and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Kentucky" title="University of Kentucky">Kentucky</a> played in the <i><a href="/wiki/Basketbowl" title="Basketbowl">Basketbowl</a></i>, in which a record crowd of 78,129 watched the game in Detroit's <a href="/wiki/Ford_Field" title="Ford Field">Ford Field</a>. Kentucky won 79–74.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> The basketball team currently plays at the <a href="/wiki/Jack_Breslin_Student_Events_Center" title="Jack Breslin Student Events Center" class="mw-redirect">Jack Breslin Student Events Center</a> under head coach <a href="/wiki/Tom_Izzo" title="Tom Izzo">Tom Izzo</a>, who has a 403–166 record as of February 2012 (70.8% winning percentage). The student spirit section at Breslin is called the <a href="/wiki/Izzone" title="Izzone">Izzone</a>. Izzo's coaching has helped the team make six <a href="/wiki/Final_Four" title="Final Four" class="mw-redirect">Final Fours</a> since 1999, winning the title in 2000, and thirteen consecutive NCAA tournament appearances (beginning in 1998). In 2009 the Spartans made it to the National Championship game and lost 89–72 to North Carolina. In 2010, the Spartans made it to the Final Four and lost 50–52 to Butler. The Spartans lost in the first round of the NCAA tournament in 2011 to UCLA 76–78.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Men.27s_ice_hockey">Men's ice hockey</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Men's ice hockey">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Munn_Ice_Arena.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/MSU_Munn_Ice_Arena.jpg/220px-MSU_Munn_Ice_Arena.jpg" width="220" height="127" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/MSU_Munn_Ice_Arena.jpg/330px-MSU_Munn_Ice_Arena.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/MSU_Munn_Ice_Arena.jpg/440px-MSU_Munn_Ice_Arena.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Munn_Ice_Arena.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Munn_Ice_Arena" title="Munn Ice Arena">Munn Ice Arena</a> was named for former 
        <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a> coach, and Athletic Director Clarence L. &quot;Biggie&quot; Munn.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_Spartans_men%27s_ice_hockey" title="Michigan State Spartans men's ice hockey">Michigan State Spartans men's ice hockey</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/Category:Michigan_State_Spartans_men%27s_ice_hockey_players" title="Category:Michigan State Spartans men's ice hockey players">Category:Michigan State Spartans men's ice hockey players</a>&nbsp;and 
      <a href="/wiki/Category:Michigan_State_Spartans_ice_hockey_coaches" title="Category:Michigan State Spartans ice hockey coaches">Category:Michigan State Spartans ice hockey coaches</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The Michigan State University men's <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> team started in 1924, though it has only been a varsity sport since 1950. The team has since won national titles in 1966, 1986 and 2007. The Spartans came close to repeating the national title in 1987, but lost the championship game to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Dakota" title="University of North Dakota">University of North Dakota</a>. They play at MSU's <a href="/wiki/Munn_Ice_Arena" title="Munn Ice Arena">Munn Ice Arena</a>. Former head coach Ron Mason is college hockey's winningest coach with 924 wins total and 635 at MSU.<sup id="cite_ref-ronmason_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ronmason-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> The current head <a href="/wiki/Coach_(ice_hockey)" title="Coach (ice hockey)">coach</a> is <a href="/wiki/Tom_Anastos" title="Tom Anastos">Tom Anastos</a>. MSU Spartans.com. Retrieved March 6, 2008.&lt;/ref&gt; Since the Big Ten Conference does not include Division I men's <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a>, Michigan State competes in the <a href="/wiki/Central_Collegiate_Hockey_Association" title="Central Collegiate Hockey Association">Central Collegiate Hockey Association</a>. Michigan State leads the CCHA in all-time wins, is second in CCHA Conference championships with 7, and is first in CCHA Tournament Championships with 11. Along with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Michigan" title="University of Michigan">University of Michigan</a> (U-M) and the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_University" title="Ohio State University">Ohio State University</a>, it is one of three Big Ten schools in the CCHA. As with other sports, the hockey rivalry between MSU and U-M is a fierce one, and on October 6, 2001, MSU faced U-M in the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War_(ice_hockey)" title="Cold War (ice hockey)">Cold War</a>, during which a world record crowd of 74,554 packed <a href="/wiki/Spartan_Stadium,_East_Lansing" title="Spartan Stadium, East Lansing" class="mw-redirect">Spartan Stadium</a> to watch the game end in a 3–3 tie.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> In the 2006–2007 season, the Men's Ice Hockey team defeated <a href="/wiki/Boston_College" title="Boston College">Boston College</a> for its third <a href="/wiki/NCAA" title="NCAA" class="mw-redirect">NCAA</a> hockey championship.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Men.27s_cross_country">Men's cross country</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Men's cross country">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_Cross_Country" title="Michigan State Cross Country" class="mw-redirect">Michigan State Cross Country</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Between World War I and World War II, Michigan State College competed in the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_Collegiate_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Central Collegiate Conference (page does not exist)">Central Collegiate Conference</a>, winning titles in 1926–1929, 1932, 1933 and 1935. Michigan State also experienced success in the <a href="/wiki/IC4A" title="IC4A">IC4A</a>, at New York's <a href="/wiki/Van_Cortlandt_Park" title="Van Cortlandt Park">Van Cortlandt Park</a>, winning 15 team titles (1933–1937, 1949, 1953, 1956–1960, 1962, 1963 and 1968). Since entering the Big Ten in 1950, Michigan State has won 14 men's team titles (1951–1953, 1955–1960, 1962, 1963, 1968, 1970 and 1971). Michigan State hosted the inaugural <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Cross_Country_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Cross Country Championship" class="mw-redirect">NCAA cross country championships</a> in 1938 and every year thereafter through 1964 (there was no championship in 1943). The Spartans won NCAA championships in 1939, 1948, 1949, 1952, 1955, 1956, 1958 and 1959.<sup id="cite_ref-Frimodig.2C_L._1971_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frimodig.2C_L._1971-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Hubbard_Hall_panoramic.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Hubbard_Hall_panoramic.jpg/220px-Hubbard_Hall_panoramic.jpg" width="220" height="107" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Hubbard_Hall_panoramic.jpg/330px-Hubbard_Hall_panoramic.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Hubbard_Hall_panoramic.jpg/440px-Hubbard_Hall_panoramic.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Hubbard_Hall_panoramic.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Hubbard Hall is a twelve-story 
        <a href="/wiki/Residence_hall" title="Residence hall" class="mw-redirect">residence hall</a> on the eastern edge of campus. It is MSU's second tallest building, surpassed by 
        <a href="/wiki/Spartan_Stadium_(East_Lansing)" title="Spartan Stadium (East Lansing)" class="mw-redirect">Spartan Stadium</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>East Lansing is very much a <a href="/wiki/College_town" title="College town">college town</a>, with 60.2% of the population between the ages of 15 and 24.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> President John A. Hannah's push to expand in the 1950s and 1960s resulted in the largest <a href="/wiki/Residence_hall" title="Residence hall" class="mw-redirect">residence hall</a> system in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> Around 16,000 students live in MSU's 23 <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_University_Housing" title="Michigan State University Housing">undergraduate halls</a>, one graduate hall, and three apartment villages. Each residence hall has its own hall government, with representatives in the <a href="/wiki/Residence_Halls_Association" title="Residence Halls Association" class="mw-redirect">Residence Halls Association</a>. Yet despite the size and extent of on-campus housing, the residence halls are complemented by a variety of housing options. 58% of students live off-campus,<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup> mostly in the areas closest to campus, in either apartment buildings, former single-family homes, fraternity and sorority houses, or in a <a href="/wiki/Student_Housing_Cooperative_at_Michigan_State_University" title="Student Housing Cooperative at Michigan State University">co-op</a>.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Union.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/MSU_Union.jpg/220px-MSU_Union.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/MSU_Union.jpg/330px-MSU_Union.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/MSU_Union.jpg/440px-MSU_Union.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Union.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_University_Student_Union" title="Michigan State University Student Union" class="mw-redirect">MSU Union</a>, designed by 
        <a href="/wiki/Pond_and_Pond" title="Pond and Pond">Pond and Pond</a> is home to many events on campus.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greek_life">Greek life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Greek life">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Michigan_State_University_fraternities_and_sororities" title="List of Michigan State University fraternities and sororities">List of Michigan State University fraternities and sororities</a>
     </div> 
     <p>With over 3,000 members, Michigan State University's <a href="/wiki/Fraternity_and_sorority_houses" title="Fraternity and sorority houses" class="mw-redirect">Greek Community</a> is one of the largest in the nation. Started in 1872<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup> and re-established in 1922 by <a href="/wiki/Lambda_Chi_Alpha" title="Lambda Chi Alpha">Lambda Chi Alpha</a> Fraternity, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Gamma_Rho" title="Alpha Gamma Rho">Alpha Gamma Rho</a> Fraternity, and <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Phi" title="Alpha Phi">Alpha Phi</a> Sorority; the MSU Greek system now consists of 55 Greek lettered student societies.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> These chapters are in turn under the jurisdiction of one of MSU's four Greek governing councils: National Panhellenic Conference, North American Interfraternity Council, National Pan-Hellenic Council,<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> and Independent Greek Council. National Pan-Hellenic Council is made up of 9 organizations, 5 Fraternities and 4 Sororities, that were founded on Historically Black College and Universities (HBCU's).<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/North-American_Interfraternity_Conference" title="North-American Interfraternity Conference">Interfraternity Council</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Panhellenic_Conference" title="National Panhellenic Conference">Women's Panhellenic Council</a> are each entirely responsible for their own budgets, giving them the freedom to hold large fundraising and recruitment events. MSU's fraternities and sororities hold many philanthropy events and community fundraisers. For example, in April 2011 the Greek Community held Greek Week to raise over $260,000 for the <a href="/wiki/American_Cancer_Society" title="American Cancer Society">American Cancer Society</a>, and $5,000 for each of these charities: <a href="/wiki/Big_Brothers_Big_Sisters_of_America" title="Big Brothers Big Sisters of America">Big Brothers Big Sisters</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Listening_Ear" title="The Listening Ear">The Listening Ear</a> and previous charities include: the <a href="/wiki/Make-A-Wish_Foundation" title="Make-A-Wish Foundation">Make-a-Wish</a> Foundation (MSU Chapter), Share Laura's Hope, The Mary Beth Knox Scholarship, and the <a href="/wiki/Special_Olympics" title="Special Olympics">Special Olympics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_organizations">Student organizations</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Student organizations">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Student_Services_Building.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Student_Services_Building.jpg/220px-Student_Services_Building.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Student_Services_Building.jpg/330px-Student_Services_Building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Student_Services_Building.jpg/440px-Student_Services_Building.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Student_Services_Building.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Student Services Building houses the MSU Department of Student Life, as well as ASMSU and the Greek governing councils.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The Associated Students of Michigan State University (ASMSU) is the undergraduate <a href="/wiki/Students%27_union" title="Students' union">student government</a> of Michigan State University.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup> It is unusual amongst university <a href="/wiki/Students%27_union" title="Students' union">student governments</a> for its <a href="/wiki/Decentralized" title="Decentralized" class="mw-redirect">decentralized</a> bicameral structure,<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup> and the relatively non-existent influence of the Greek system. ASMSU representatives are <a href="/wiki/Nonpartisan" title="Nonpartisan">nonpartisan</a> and many are elected in noncompetitive races. Their mission is to enhance the individual and collective student experience through education, empowerment, and advocacy by education to the needs and interest of students. Some services they offer include: free blue books, low cost copies and faxes, free yearbooks, interest free loans, funding for student organizations, free legal consultation, health insurance, and iClicker rentals. There are many ways of getting involved such as: Freshman Class Council, Senior Class Council, appointments to General Assembly, and employment.</p> 
     <p>Students pay $16.75 per semester to fund the functions of the ASMSU, including stipends for the organization's officers and activities throughout the year.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> Some students have criticized ASMSU for not having enough electoral participation to gain a student mandate. <a href="/wiki/Voter_turnout" title="Voter turnout">Turnout</a> since 2001 has hovered between 3 and 17 percent, with the 2006 election bringing out 8% of the undergraduate student body.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Student-run organizations beyond student government also have a large impact on the East Lansing/Michigan State University community. Student Organizations are registered through the Department of Student Life, which currently has a registry of over 550 student organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> One example is the <a href="/wiki/Tower_Guard" title="Tower Guard" class="mw-redirect">Tower Guard</a> honor society. Tower Guard is the oldest and one of the most respected student organizations on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Eli Broad College of Business includes 27 student organizations. The three largest organizations are the Finance Association (FA), the Accounting Student Association (ASA), and the Supply Chain Management Association (SCMA).<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup> The SCMA is the host of the university's largest major specific career fair. The fair attracts over 100 companies and over 400 students each year.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Activism">Activism</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Activism">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Activism" title="Activism">Activists</a> have played a significant role in MSU history. During the height of the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a>, student protests helped create <a href="/wiki/Co-ed" title="Co-ed" class="mw-redirect">co-ed</a> residence halls, and blocked the routing of <a href="/wiki/Interstate_496" title="Interstate 496">Interstate 496</a> through campus.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup> In the 1980s, Michigan State students convinced the University to <a href="/wiki/Divestment" title="Divestment">divest</a> the stocks of companies doing business in <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid" class="mw-redirect">apartheid</a> South Africa from its endowment portfolio, such as <a href="/wiki/The_Coca-Cola_Company" title="The Coca-Cola Company">Coca-Cola</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup> MSU has many student groups focused on political change. Graduate campus groups include the Graduate Employees Union<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup> and the Council of Graduate Students.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup> Michigan State also has a variety of partisan groups ranging from liberal to conservative, including the <a href="/wiki/College_Republicans" title="College Republicans">College Republicans</a>, the <a href="/wiki/College_Democrats" title="College Democrats" class="mw-redirect">College Democrats</a> and several <a href="/wiki/Third_party_(politics)" title="Third party (politics)">third party</a> organizations. Other partisan activist groups include <a href="/wiki/Young_Americans_for_Freedom" title="Young Americans for Freedom">Young Americans for Freedom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Young_Americans_for_Liberty" title="Young Americans for Liberty">Young Americans for Liberty</a> on the right; <a href="/wiki/Young_Democratic_Socialists" title="Young Democratic Socialists">Young Democratic Socialists</a>, Students for Economic Justice, <a href="/wiki/Young_Communist_League" title="Young Communist League">Young Communist League</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/Movimiento_Estudiantil_Chicano_de_Aztlan" title="Movimiento Estudiantil Chicano de Aztlan" class="mw-redirect">MEChA</a></i> on the left. Given MSU's proximity to the Michigan state capital of <a href="/wiki/Lansing,_Michigan" title="Lansing, Michigan">Lansing</a>, many politically inclined Spartans intern for state representatives.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sustainability">Sustainability</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Sustainability">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The MSU Office of Sustainability works with the University Committee for a Sustainable Campus to &quot;foster a collaborative learning culture that leads the community to heightened awareness of its environmental impact.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-The_Office_of_Campus_Sustainability_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Office_of_Campus_Sustainability-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup> The University is a member of the Chicago Climate Exchange, the world's first greenhouse gas emission registry, and boasts the lowest electrical consumption per square foot among <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten" title="Big Ten" class="mw-redirect">Big Ten</a> universities. The University has set a goal of reducing energy use by 15%, reducing greenhouse gas emissions by 15%, reducing landfill waste by 30% by 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-MSU_honored_by_National_Wildlife_Federation_for_sustainability_efforts_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSU_honored_by_National_Wildlife_Federation_for_sustainability_efforts-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university has also pledged to meet <a href="/wiki/Leadership_in_Energy_and_Environmental_Design" title="Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design">LEED</a>-certification standards for all new construction. In July 2009, the University completed construction of a $13.3 million recycling center, and hopes to double their 2008 recycling rate of 14% by 2010. <sup id="cite_ref-MSU_Board_of_Trustees_OKs_.2413.3M_step_to_go_.27green.27_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSU_Board_of_Trustees_OKs_.2413.3M_step_to_go_.27green.27-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup> The construction of Brody Hall, a residence hall of Michigan State University Housing, was completed in August 2011 and qualified for LEED Silver certification because the facility includes a rain water collection tank used for restroom fixtures, a white PVC roof, meters that will monitor utilities to make sure they are used efficiently, and the use of recycled matter and local sources for building materials.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Environmental Steward's program support's president Simon's &quot;Boldness by Design&quot; strategic vision to transform environmental stewardship on campus within the seven-year time frame.<sup id="cite_ref-Environmental_Stewardship_Program_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Environmental_Stewardship_Program-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup> Environmental stewards promote environmental changes among co-workers and peers, be points of contact for their department for environment-related concerns, and be liaisons between the Be Spartan Green Team and buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-Environmental_Stewardship_Program_164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Environmental_Stewardship_Program-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>ECO is the leading student-run sustainability organization on campus. They are also affiliated with regional and national groups such as Campus Climate Challenge and the Michigan Student Sustainability Coalition.<sup id="cite_ref-MSU_ECO_Get_Involved_On_Campus_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSU_ECO_Get_Involved_On_Campus-165"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Student Organic Farm is a student-run, four-season farm, which teaches the principals of organic farming and through a certificate program and <a href="/wiki/Community_supported_agriculture" title="Community supported agriculture" class="mw-redirect">community supported agriculture</a> (CSA) on ten acres on the MSU campus.<sup id="cite_ref-MSU_Organic_Farm_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSU_Organic_Farm-166"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup> The certificate program consists of year round crop production, course work in organic farming, practical training and management, and an off-site internship requirement.<sup id="cite_ref-Certificate_Program_Overview_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Certificate_Program_Overview-167"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Bronze_Sparty_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4b/MSU_Bronze_Sparty_2.jpg/170px-MSU_Bronze_Sparty_2.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/4/4b/MSU_Bronze_Sparty_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/4/4b/MSU_Bronze_Sparty_2.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Bronze_Sparty_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> A 2005 bronze replica of &quot;The Spartan&quot; (nicknamed &quot;
        <a href="/wiki/Sparty" title="Sparty">Sparty</a>&quot;) replaces Leonard D. Jungwirth's 
        <a href="/wiki/Modernist" title="Modernist" class="mw-redirect">modernist</a> original.
        <sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>MSU has a variety of campus media outlets. The student-run newspaper is called <i><a href="/wiki/The_State_News" title="The State News">The State News</a></i> and free copies of the paper are available online or at East Lansing newsstands. The paper prints 28,500 copies of the paper Monday through Friday during the fall and spring semesters, and 15,000 copies Monday through Friday during the summer.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup> The paper is not published on weekends, holidays, or semester breaks, but is continually updated online at statenews.com. The campus <a href="/wiki/Yearbook" title="Yearbook">yearbook</a> is called the <i>Red Cedar Log</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Red Cedar Review</i>, Michigan State University's premier literary digest for over forty years, is the longest running undergraduate-run literary journal in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup> It is published annually by the <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_University_Press" title="Michigan State University Press">Michigan State University Press</a>.</p> 
     <p>MSU also publishes a student-run magazine during the academic year called Ing Magazine.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup> Created in 2007 by MSU alumnus Adam Grant, the publication is released at the beginning of each month and currently publishes 7 issues each school year.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Electronic media include three radio stations and one <a href="/wiki/Public_television" title="Public television" class="mw-redirect">public television</a> station, as well as <a href="/wiki/MSU_Telecasters" title="MSU Telecasters">student-produced</a> television shows. MSU's <a href="/wiki/Public_Broadcasting_Service" title="Public Broadcasting Service" class="mw-redirect">Public Broadcasting Service</a> affiliate, <a href="/wiki/WKAR-TV" title="WKAR-TV">WKAR-TV</a>, the station is the second-oldest educational television station in the United States, and the oldest east of the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a>. Besides broadcasting PBS shows, WKAR-TV produces its own local programming, such as a high school <a href="/wiki/Quiz_bowl" title="Quiz bowl">quiz bowl</a> show called &quot;QuizBusters&quot;. In addition, MSU has three radio stations; WKAR-AM plays <a href="/wiki/National_Public_Radio" title="National Public Radio" class="mw-redirect">National Public Radio</a>'s talk radio programming, whereas WKAR-FM focuses mostly on classical music programming.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup> Michigan State's student-run radio station, <a href="/wiki/WDBM" title="WDBM">WDBM</a>, broadcasts mostly alternative music during weekdays, and electric music programming nights and weekends.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_forest_trail.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/MSU_forest_trail.jpg/170px-MSU_forest_trail.jpg" width="170" height="209" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/MSU_forest_trail.jpg/255px-MSU_forest_trail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/MSU_forest_trail.jpg/340px-MSU_forest_trail.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_forest_trail.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> MSU's campus is heavily forested. This trail runs behind several residence halls, including Owen Hall, McDonel Hall and Holmes Hall.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="People">People</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: People">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Michigan_State_University_people" title="List of Michigan State University people">List of Michigan State University people</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The current president of the University is <a href="/wiki/Lou_Anna_Simon" title="Lou Anna Simon">Lou Anna Simon</a> who took over on January 1, 2005, after being appointed by MSU's governing board, the <a href="/wiki/Board_of_Trustees" title="Board of Trustees" class="mw-redirect">Board of Trustees</a>. The Board receives its mandate from the Michigan Constitution since MSU is a state-owned school. The constitution allows for eight <a href="/wiki/Trustee" title="Trustee">trustees</a> who are elected by statewide referendum every two years. Trustees have eight-year terms, with two of the eight elected every other year.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup> As of 2007, the Board is made up of three <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republicans</a> and five <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democrats</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="19th_century">19th century</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: 19th century">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Eustace-Cole_Hall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/MSU_Eustace-Cole_Hall.jpg/220px-MSU_Eustace-Cole_Hall.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/MSU_Eustace-Cole_Hall.jpg/330px-MSU_Eustace-Cole_Hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/MSU_Eustace-Cole_Hall.jpg/440px-MSU_Eustace-Cole_Hall.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Eustace-Cole_Hall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Eustace-Cole_Hall" title="Eustace-Cole Hall" class="mw-redirect">Eustace-Cole Hall</a> was the United States' first freestanding horticulture laboratory. It is the only MSU building on the 
        <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a>. Additionally, Eustace-Cole Hall houses the offices of the Michigan State University Honors College.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Important College leaders in the 19th century include <a href="/wiki/John_Clough_Holmes" title="John Clough Holmes">John C. Holmes</a>, who kept the Agriculture School from being a part of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Michigan" title="University of Michigan">University of Michigan</a> and is widely credited with being the prime mover for the school's founding;<sup id="cite_ref-sesquicentennial_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sesquicentennial-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Joseph_R._Williams" title="Joseph R. Williams">Joseph R. Williams</a>, the first president;<sup id="cite_ref-josephrwilliams_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-josephrwilliams-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Theophilus_C._Abbot" title="Theophilus C. Abbot">Theophilus C. Abbot</a>, the third president who stabilized the College after the Civil War.<sup id="cite_ref-tcabbot_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tcabbot-178"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup> Also of importance was botany professor <a href="/wiki/William_J._Beal" title="William J. Beal" class="mw-redirect">William J. Beal</a>, an early plant (hybrid corn) geneticist who championed the laboratory teaching method.<sup id="cite_ref-williamjbeal_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-williamjbeal-179"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup> Another distinguished faculty member of the era was the alumnus/professor <a href="/wiki/Liberty_Hyde_Bailey" title="Liberty Hyde Bailey">Liberty Hyde Bailey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-libertyhydebailey_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-libertyhydebailey-180"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup> Bailey was the first to raise the study of horticulture to a science, paralleling botany, which earned him the title of &quot;Father of American Horticulture&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/William_L._Carpenter_(Michigan_jurist)" title="William L. Carpenter (Michigan jurist)">William L. Carpenter</a>, a jurist who was elected to the Third Judicial Circuit of Michigan in 1894, and member of the <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Supreme_Court" title="Michigan Supreme Court">Michigan Supreme Court</a> from 1902 until 1904. Other famous 19th century graduates include <a href="/wiki/Ray_Stannard_Baker" title="Ray Stannard Baker">Ray Stannard Baker</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-raystannardbaker_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-raystannardbaker-182"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup> a famed &quot;<a href="/wiki/Muckraker" title="Muckraker">muckraker</a>&quot; journalist and <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> winning biographer; <a href="/wiki/Minakata_Kumagusu" title="Minakata Kumagusu">Minakata Kumagusu</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-minakatakumagusu_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-minakatakumagusu-183"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup> a renowned environmental scientist; and <a href="/wiki/William_Bagley_(educator)" title="William Bagley (educator)">William Chandler Bagley</a>, a pioneering education reformer.<sup id="cite_ref-williamcbagley_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-williamcbagley-184"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Human_Ecology_Building.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2b/MSU_Human_Ecology_Building.jpg/220px-MSU_Human_Ecology_Building.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2b/MSU_Human_Ecology_Building.jpg/330px-MSU_Human_Ecology_Building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2b/MSU_Human_Ecology_Building.jpg/440px-MSU_Human_Ecology_Building.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:MSU_Human_Ecology_Building.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Human Ecology Building
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_and_21st_centuries">20th and 21st centuries</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Michigan_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: 20th and 21st centuries">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>There are currently around 442,000 living MSU <a href="/wiki/Alumni" title="Alumni" class="mw-redirect">alumni</a> worldwide giving the school one of the largest number of alumni of any institution of higher learning.<sup id="cite_ref-msufacts_3-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-msufacts-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> Famous MSU alumni include former Michigan governors <a href="/wiki/James_Blanchard" title="James Blanchard">James Blanchard</a><sup id="cite_ref-jamesblanchard_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jamesblanchard-185"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/John_Engler" title="John Engler">John Engler</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-johnengler_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-johnengler-186"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup> U.S. Senators <a href="/wiki/Debbie_Stabenow" title="Debbie Stabenow">Debbie Stabenow</a><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Tim_Johnson_(U.S._Senator)" title="Tim Johnson (U.S. Senator)">Tim Johnson</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Ambassador_to_Brazil" title="U.S. Ambassador to Brazil" class="mw-redirect">U.S. Ambassador to Brazil</a> <a href="/wiki/Donna_Hrinak" title="Donna Hrinak">Donna Hrinak</a>, former <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Jordan" title="Prime Minister of Jordan">Jordan prime minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Adnan_Badran" title="Adnan Badran">Adnan Badran</a>, billionaire philanthropists <a href="/wiki/Tom_Gores" title="Tom Gores">Tom Gores</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eli_Broad" title="Eli Broad">Eli Broad</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-elibroad_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elibroad-188"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chief_Justice" title="Chief Justice">Chief Justice</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Texas" title="Supreme Court of Texas">Texas Supreme Court</a> <a href="/wiki/Wallace_B._Jefferson" title="Wallace B. Jefferson">Wallace B. Jefferson</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Wallace_B._Jefferson_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wallace_B._Jefferson-189"><span>[</span>189<span>]</span></a></sup> trial lawyer <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Feiger" title="Geoffrey Feiger" class="mw-redirect">Geoffrey Feiger</a>, former <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Drug_Administration" title="Food and Drug Administration">Food and Drug Administration</a> official <a href="/wiki/Peter_Rheinstein" title="Peter Rheinstein">Peter Rheinstein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a>-winning novelist <a href="/wiki/Richard_Ford" title="Richard Ford">Richard Ford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Teamsters" title="Teamsters" class="mw-redirect">Teamsters</a> president <a href="/wiki/James_P._Hoffa" title="James P. Hoffa">James P. Hoffa</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-jamesphoffa_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jamesphoffa-190"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Quicken_Loans" title="Quicken Loans">Quicken Loans</a> founder and <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Cavaliers" title="Cleveland Cavaliers">Cleveland Cavaliers</a> owner and billionaire <a href="/wiki/Dan_Gilbert_(businessman)" title="Dan Gilbert (businessman)">Dan Gilbert</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-dangilbert_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dangilbert-191"><span>[</span>191<span>]</span></a></sup> Sergeant at Arms of the U.S. House of Representatives <a href="/wiki/Wilson_Livingood" title="Wilson Livingood">Wilson Livingood</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-wilsonlivingood_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wilsonlivingood-192"><span>[</span>192<span>]</span></a></sup> former Michigan U.S. Senator and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_Energy" title="United States Secretary of Energy">Secretary of Energy</a> <a href="/wiki/Spencer_Abraham" title="Spencer Abraham">Spencer Abraham</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-spencerabraham_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spencerabraham-193"><span>[</span>193<span>]</span></a></sup> former Vice President of the Republic of Liberia <a href="/wiki/Harry_Moniba" title="Harry Moniba">Harry Moniba</a>, and former U.S. Ambassador to Italy <a href="/wiki/Peter_Secchia" title="Peter Secchia" class="mw-redirect">Peter Secchia</a>. Alumni in Hollywood include actors such as <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Heald" title="Anthony Heald">Anthony Heald</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-anthonyheald_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-anthonyheald-194"><span>[</span>194<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Urich" title="Robert Urich">Robert Urich</a><sup id="cite_ref-roberturich_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roberturich-195"><span>[</span>195<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/William_Fawcett_(actor)" title="William Fawcett (actor)">William Fawcett</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-williamfawcett_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-williamfawcett-196"><span>[</span>196<span>]</span></a></sup> comedian <a href="/wiki/Dick_Martin_(comedian)" title="Dick Martin (comedian)">Dick Martin</a>, comedian <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Martling" title="Jackie Martling">Jackie Martling</a>, film directors <a href="/wiki/Michael_Cimino" title="Michael Cimino">Michael Cimino</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sam_Raimi" title="Sam Raimi">Sam Raimi</a>, and film editor <a href="/wiki/Bob_Murawski" title="Bob Murawski">Bob Murawski</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-bobmurawski_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bobmurawski-197"><span>[</span>197<span>]</span></a></sup> as well as screenwriter <a href="/wiki/David_Magee" title="David Magee">David Magee</a><sup id="cite_ref-davidmagee_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-davidmagee-198"><span>[</span>198<span>]</span></a></sup> Puerto Rican comedian <a href="/wiki/Sunshine_Logro%C3%B1o" title="Sunshine Logro&ntilde;o">Sunshine Logro&ntilde;o</a> (who has played the occasional Hollywood movie) was a graduate student at MSU. Journalists include NBC reporter <a href="/wiki/Chris_Hansen" title="Chris Hansen">Chris Hansen</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199"><span>[</span>199<span>]</span></a></sup> AP White House correspondent <a href="/wiki/Nedra_Pickler" title="Nedra Pickler">Nedra Pickler</a>, and <a href="/wiki/NPR" title="NPR">NPR</a> Washington correspondent <a href="/wiki/Don_Gonyea" title="Don Gonyea">Don Gonyea</a>. Novelist <a href="/wiki/Michael_Kimball" title="Michael Kimball">Michael Kimball</a> graduated in 1990. Novelist and true crime author <a href="/wiki/R._Barri_Flowers" title="R. Barri Flowers">R. Barri Flowers</a>, who in 1977 a bachelors and in 1980 a masters in criminal justice, was inducted in 2006 into the MSU Criminal Justice Wall of Fame.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200"><span>[</span>200<span>]</span></a></sup> Author <a href="/wiki/Erik_Qualman" title="Erik Qualman">Erik Qualman</a> graduated with honors in 1994 and was also Academic Big-Ten in basketball. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Susan_K._Avery&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Susan K. Avery (page does not exist)">Susan K. Avery</a>, the first woman president and director of the <a href="/wiki/Woods_Hole_Oceanographic_Institution" title="Woods Hole Oceanographic Institution">Woods Hole Oceanographic Institution</a>, received an MSU bachelor's degree in <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">physics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201"><span>[</span>201<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, two of the <a href="/wiki/Little_Rock_Nine" title="Little Rock Nine">Little Rock Nine</a> attended Michigan State, including <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Green" title="Ernest Green">Ernest Green</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-ernestgreen_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ernestgreen-202"><span>[</span>202<span>]</span></a></sup> the first black student to graduate from <a href="/wiki/Little_Rock_Central_High_School" title="Little Rock Central High School">Little Rock Central High School</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Carlotta_Walls_LaNier" title="Carlotta Walls LaNier">Carlotta Walls LaNier</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-carlottawellslanier_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carlottawellslanier-203"><span>[</span>203<span>]</span></a></sup> The University awarded an honorary degree to <a href="/wiki/Robert_Mugabe" title="Robert Mugabe">Robert Mugabe</a> in 1990, but revoked it in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204"><span>[</span>204<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Spartans formerly or currently in the <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">NBA</a> include <a href="/wiki/Earvin_%22Magic%22_Johnson" title="Earvin &quot;Magic&quot; Johnson" class="mw-redirect">Earvin &quot;Magic&quot; Johnson</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-magicjohnson_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-magicjohnson-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Greg_Kelser" title="Greg Kelser">Greg Kelser</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-gregkelser_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gregkelser-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jay_Vincent" title="Jay Vincent">Jay Vincent</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-jayvincent_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jayvincent-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Steve_Smith_(basketball)" title="Steve Smith (basketball)">Steve Smith</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-stevesmith_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stevesmith-205"><span>[</span>205<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Scott_Skiles" title="Scott Skiles">Scott Skiles</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-scottskiles_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scottskiles-206"><span>[</span>206<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jason_Richardson" title="Jason Richardson">Jason Richardson</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-jasonrichardson_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jasonrichardson-207"><span>[</span>207<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mateen_Cleaves" title="Mateen Cleaves">Mateen Cleaves</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-mateencleaves_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mateencleaves-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alan_Anderson_(basketball)" title="Alan Anderson (basketball)">Alan Anderson</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-alanderson_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alanderson-208"><span>[</span>208<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Zach_Randolph" title="Zach Randolph">Zach Randolph</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-zachrandolph_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zachrandolph-209"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Morris_Peterson" title="Morris Peterson">Morris Peterson</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-morrispeterson_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-morrispeterson-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Bell_(basketball)" title="Charlie Bell (basketball)">Charlie Bell</a><sup id="cite_ref-charliebell_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charliebell-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Shannon_Brown" title="Shannon Brown">Shannon Brown</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-shannonbrown_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shannonbrown-210"><span>[</span>210<span>]</span></a></sup> On the <a href="/wiki/American_Football_League" title="American Football League">American Football League</a>'s <a href="/wiki/American_Football_League_All-Time_Team" title="American Football League All-Time Team">All-Time Team</a> are tight-end <a href="/wiki/Fred_Arbanas" title="Fred Arbanas">Fred Arbanas</a><sup id="cite_ref-fredarbansas_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fredarbansas-211"><span>[</span>211<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Safety_(American_football_position)" title="Safety (American football position)" class="mw-redirect">safety</a> <a href="/wiki/George_Saimes" title="George Saimes">George Saimes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-georgesaimes_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-georgesaimes-212"><span>[</span>212<span>]</span></a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a>, MSU alumni include Carl Banks, who was a member of the Giants teams that won <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXI" title="Super Bowl XXI">Super Bowls XXI</a> and <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXV" title="Super Bowl XXV">XXV</a>. Banks was a standout in their Super Bowl XXI victory in which he recorded 14 total tackles, including ten solo tackles, as well as being part of the NFL's 1980's All-Decade Team <a href="/wiki/Morten_Andersen" title="Morten Andersen">Morten Andersen</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-mortenandersen_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mortenandersen-213"><span>[</span>213<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Plaxico_Burress" title="Plaxico Burress">Plaxico Burress</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-plaxicoburress_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plaxicoburress-214"><span>[</span>214<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Andre_Rison" title="Andre Rison">Andre Rison</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-andrerison_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-andrerison-215"><span>[</span>215<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Derrick_Mason" title="Derrick Mason">Derrick Mason</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-derrickmason_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-derrickmason-216"><span>[</span>216<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Muhsin_Muhammad" title="Muhsin Muhammad">Muhsin Muhammad</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-muhsinmuhammad_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-muhsinmuhammad-217"><span>[</span>217<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/T._J._Duckett" title="T. J. Duckett">T. J. Duckett</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-tjduckett_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tjduckett-218"><span>[</span>218<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Flozell_Adams" title="Flozell Adams">Flozell Adams</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-flozelladams_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flozelladams-219"><span>[</span>219<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Julian_Peterson" title="Julian Peterson">Julian Peterson</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-julianpeterson_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-julianpeterson-220"><span>[</span>220<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Charles_Rogers_(American_football)" title="Charles Rogers (American football)">Charles Rogers</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-charlesrogers_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charlesrogers-221"><span>[</span>221<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jim_Miller_(quarterback)" title="Jim Miller (quarterback)">Jim Miller</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-jimmiller_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jimmiller-222"><span>[</span>222<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Earl_Morrall" title="Earl Morrall">Earl Morrall</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-earlmorrall_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earlmorrall-223"><span>[</span>223<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Fontes" title="Wayne Fontes">Wayne Fontes</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-waynefontes_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-waynefontes-224"><span>[</span>224<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bubba_Smith" title="Bubba Smith">Bubba Smith</a><sup id="cite_ref-bubbasmith_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bubbasmith-225"><span>[</span>225<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Drew_Stanton" title="Drew Stanton">Drew Stanton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-drewstanton_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drewstanton-226"><span>[</span>226<span>]</span></a></sup> Former MSU quarterback <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Smoker" title="Jeff Smoker">Jeff Smoker</a> now plays in the <a href="/wiki/Arena_Football_League_(1987%E2%80%932008)" title="Arena Football League (1987–2008)" class="mw-redirect">Arena Football League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-jeffsmoker_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jeffsmoker-227"><span>[</span>227<span>]</span></a></sup> Former Michigan State players in the <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">National Hockey League</a> include All Star Defensemen <a href="/wiki/Duncan_Keith" title="Duncan Keith">Duncan Keith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rod_Brind%27Amour" title="Rod Brind'Amour">Rod Brind'Amour</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-rodbrindamour_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rodbrindamour-228"><span>[</span>228<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Anson_Carter" title="Anson Carter">Anson Carter</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-ansoncarter_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ansoncarter-229"><span>[</span>229<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Donald_McSween" title="Donald McSween">Donald McSween</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-donaldmcsween_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-donaldmcsween-230"><span>[</span>230<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Adam_Hall" title="Adam Hall">Adam Hall</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-adamhall_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-adamhall-231"><span>[</span>231<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John-Michael_Liles" title="John-Michael Liles">John-Michael Liles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Justin_Abdelkader" title="Justin Abdelkader">Justin Abdelkader</a>, brothers <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Miller_(ice_hockey_b._1963)" title="Kelly Miller (ice hockey b. 1963)">Kelly Miller</a><sup id="cite_ref-kellymiller_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kellymiller-232"><span>[</span>232<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Kip_Miller" title="Kip Miller">Kip Miller</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-kipmiller_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kipmiller-233"><span>[</span>233<span>]</span></a></sup> as well as their cousins, brothers <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Miller" title="Ryan Miller">Ryan Miller</a><sup id="cite_ref-ryanmiller_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ryanmiller-234"><span>[</span>234<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Drew_Miller" title="Drew Miller">Drew Miller</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-drewmiller_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drewmiller-235"><span>[</span>235<span>]</span></a></sup> Former Michigan State players in <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> include <a href="/wiki/National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum" title="National Baseball Hall of Fame and Museum">Hall of Fame</a> inductee <a href="/wiki/Robin_Roberts_(baseball_player)" title="Robin Roberts (baseball player)" class="mw-redirect">Robin Roberts</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-robinroberts_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-robinroberts-236"><span>[</span>236<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kirk_Gibson" title="Kirk Gibson">Kirk Gibson</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-kirkgibson_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kirkgibson-237"><span>[</span>237<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Steve_Garvey" title="Steve Garvey">Steve Garvey</a><sup id="cite_ref-stevegarvey_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stevegarvey-238"><span>[</span>238<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Mark_Mulder" title="Mark Mulder">Mark Mulder</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-markmulder_239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-markmulder-239"><span>[</span>239<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Olympic_gold_medal" title="Olympic gold medal" class="mw-redirect">Olympic gold medalists</a> include <a href="/wiki/Savatheda_Fynes" title="Savatheda Fynes">Savatheda Fynes</a><sup id="cite_ref-sevathedafynes_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sevathedafynes-240"><span>[</span>240<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Fred_Alderman" title="Fred Alderman">Fred Alderman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-frederickalderman_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frederickalderman-241"><span>[</span>241<span>]</span></a></sup> The Spartans are also contributing athletes to <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Soccer" title="Major League Soccer">Major League Soccer</a>, as <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kevin_Reiman&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kevin Reiman (page does not exist)">Kevin Reiman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doug_DeMartin" title="Doug DeMartin">Doug DeMartin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dave_Hertel" title="Dave Hertel">Dave Hertel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greg_Janicki" title="Greg Janicki">Greg Janicki</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kenzo_Webster&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kenzo Webster (page does not exist)">Kenzo Webster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rauwshan_McKenzie" title="Rauwshan McKenzie">Rauwshan McKenzie</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=John_Minagawa-Webster&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="John Minagawa-Webster (page does not exist)">John Minagawa-Webster</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ryan_McMahen" title="Ryan McMahen">Ryan McMahen</a> have all played in <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Soccer" title="Major League Soccer">Major League Soccer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242"><span>[</span>242<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, <a href="/wiki/Alex_Skotarek" title="Alex Skotarek">Alex Skotarek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steve_Twellman" title="Steve Twellman">Steve Twellman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Buzz_Demling" title="Buzz Demling">Buzz Demling</a> played in the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Soccer_League" title="North American Soccer League">North American Soccer League</a>, with Demling playing in the <a href="/wiki/1972_Summer_Olympics" title="1972 Summer Olympics">1972 Summer Olympics</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Men%27s_National_Soccer_Team" title="United States Men's National Soccer Team" class="mw-redirect">United States Men's National Soccer Team</a> in the 1970s.</p>
